ANDERSON

13 Dec 1801
ANDERSON created from GRAINGER, KNOX, and Non-County Area 2. (Tenn. Acts 1801, 4th assy., ch. 45, secs. 1, 2, 4, 30/pp. 274, 279)
11 Sep 1806
ANDERSON lost to creation of CAMPBELL. (Scott, ch. 21, sec. 1/p. 945)
07 Nov 1807
ANDERSON exchanged with CAMPBELL. (Tenn. Acts 1807, 7th assy., 1st sess., ch. 51, secs. 1-2/p. 86)
28 Oct 1811
ANDERSON lost to CAMPBELL [repealed 17 November 1813]. (Tenn. Acts 1811, 9th assy., 1st sess., ch. 56/p. 62)
17 Nov 1813
ANDERSON gained from CAMPBELL [repealed act of 28 October 1811]. (Tenn. Acts 1813, 10th assy., ch. 101/p. 137)
24 Sep 1817
ANDERSON lost to CAMPBELL. (Tenn. Acts 1817, 12th assy., ch. 20/p. 24)
01 Jan 1818
ANDERSON lost to creation of MORGAN; gained from ROANE. (Tenn. Acts 1817, 12th assy., ch. 38, secs. 1, 18/pp. 41, 45 and ch. 81/p. 89)
17 Dec 1849
ANDERSON lost to creation of SCOTT. (Tenn. Acts 1849, 28th assy., ch. 45, secs. 1-2, 4/pp. 145, 147)
26 Jan 1854
ANDERSON lost to creation of UNION. (Tenn. Acts 1849, 28th assy., ch. 61, secs. 1-2, 4, 18/pp. 181-187; Tenn. Acts 1851, 29th assy., ch. 22/p. 26; Tenn. Acts 1853, 30th assy., ch. 2, secs. 1-2/pp. 25-26; Graves, 1:68-69)
11 Feb 1854
ANDERSON gained from SCOTT. (Tenn. Acts 1853, 30th assy., ch. 320, secs. 1-2, 10, 21, 24-25/pp. 744-754)
20 Feb 1854
ANDERSON lost to CAMPBELL [loss apparently included the area ANDERSON gained from SCOTT on 11 February 1854]. (Tenn. Acts 1853, 30th assy., ch. 129/p. 203)
22 Feb 1856
ANDERSON lost to ROANE to accommodate local residents [change too small to display on interactive map; shapefile users see small_changes 1856_pt. for location]. (Tenn. Acts 1855, 31st assy., ch. 161/p. 244)
04 Mar 1858
Legislature authorized ROANE to gain from ANDERSON effective 1 May 1858 [repealed 20 March 1858, no change]. (Tenn. Acts 1857, 32d assy., pub., ch. 47, secs. 1-11/pp. 57-59 and ch. 83, sec. 3/p. 91)
15 Mar 1858
ANDERSON lost small area to ROANE [repealed 7 July 1870; change too small to display on interactive map; shapefile users see small_changes 1858_pt. for location]. (Tenn. Acts 1857, 32d assy., priv., ch. 129/p. 324)
20 Mar 1858
Act of 4 March 1858 authorizing ROANE to gain from ANDERSON was repealed [no change]. (Tenn. Acts 1857, 32d assy., pub., ch. 83, secs. 1-4, 8-9/pp. 91-93)
08 Jun 1865
ANDERSON gained from CAMPBELL to accommodate local resident [location unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1865, 34th assy., 1st sess., priv., ch. 29/p. 112)
07 Mar 1868
ANDERSON lost to CAMPBELL to accommodate local resident [repealed 27 January 1905; location unknown, not mapped] (Tenn. Acts 1867, 35th assy., 1st sess., pub., ch. 60/p. 75)
19 Feb 1869
ANDERSON lost to CAMPBELL to accommodate local resident [location unknown, not mapped] (Tenn. Acts 1868, 35th assy., 2d sess., pub., ch. 36/p. 48)
07 Jul 1870
ANDERSON gained small area from ROANE [repealed act of 15 March 1858; change too small to display on interactive map; shapefile users see small_changes 1870_pt. for location]. (Tenn. Acts 1870, 36th assy., 2d sess., ch. 88/p. 137)
24 Mar 1873
ANDERSON lost to SCOTT to accommodate local residents. (Tenn. Acts 1873, 38th assy., ch. 75/p. 109)
12 Mar 1883
ANDERSON lost to CAMPBELL to accommodate local resident [change too small to display on interactive map; shapefile users see small_changes 1883_pt. for location]. (Tenn. Acts 1883, 43d assy., ch. 51/p. 54)
02 Mar 1887
ANDERSON gained from CAMPBELL to accommodate local residents [repealed 1 April 1893; locations unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1887, 45th assy., ch. 35/p. 106)
25 Mar 1887
Legislature authorized ANDERSON to gain from ROANE, but ROANE would not accept survey [no change]. (Tenn. Acts 1887, 45th assy., ch. 127/p. 226; "Roane County v. Anderson County" in Tenn. Rpts., 89:259-269)
27 Feb 1889
ANDERSON gained small area from ROANE [overturned by Tennessee Supreme Court, 11 October 1890; change too small to display on interactive map; shapefile users see small_changes 1889_pt. for location]. (Tenn. Acts 1889, 46th assy., 1st sess., ch. 34/p. 62)
22 Mar 1889
ANDERSON gained Holt Island from KNOX to accommodate local resident [change too small to display on interactive map; shapefile users see small_changes 1889_pt. for location]. (Tenn. Acts 1889, 46th assy., 1st sess., ch. 124/p. 229)
11 Oct 1890
ANDERSON lost small area to ROANE when Tennessee Supreme Court overturned act of 27 February 1889 [change too small to display on interactive map; shapefile users see small_changes 1890_pt. for location]. ("Roane County v. Anderson County" in Tenn. Rpts., 89:259-269)
01 Apr 1893
ANDERSON lost to CAMPBELL to accommodate local residents [repealed act of 2 March 1887; location unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1893, 48th assy., ch. 60/p. 77)
21 Apr 1899
ANDERSON lost to ROANE to accommodate local resident [location unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1899, 51st assy., ch. 317/p. 752)
02 Apr 1903
ANDERSON lost small area to MORGAN. (Tenn. Acts 1903, 53d assy., ch. 304/p. 883; repeated in ch. 504/p. 1347)
27 Jan 1905
ANDERSON gained from CAMPBELL to accommodate local resident [repealed act of 7 March 1868; location unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1905, 54th assy., ch. 53/p. 98)
24 Mar 1919
ANDERSON gained from CAMPBELL [repealed 22 April 1933]. (Tenn. Acts 1919, 61st assy., priv., ch. 95/p. 204)
22 Apr 1927
ANDERSON lost to CAMPBELL to accommodate local resident [location unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1927, 65th assy., priv., ch. 398/p. 1145)
22 Apr 1933
ANDERSON lost to CAMPBELL [repealed act of 24 March 1919]. (Tenn. Acts 1933, 68th assy., priv., ch. 612/p. 1459)

BEDFORD

03 Dec 1807
BEDFORD created from RUTHERFORD and WILLIAMSON. (Tenn. Acts 1807, 7th assy., 1st sess., ch. 37, sec. 1/p. 71)
01 Dec 1809
BEDFORD gained from WILLIAMSON. (Scott, ch. 37/p. 1141)
01 Jan 1810
BEDFORD lost to creation of LINCOLN and lost to FRANKLIN. (Scott, ch. 43/pp. 1147-1148 and ch. 51/pp. 1158-1160)
20 Aug 1822

BELL (proposed)

20 Dec 1870
Legislature authorized creation of BELL from FAYETTE, HARDEMAN, and McNAIRY; voided by Tennessee Supreme Court, 8 June 1871. (Tenn. Acts 1870, 36th assy., 3d sess., ch. 16, secs. 1-2,4/pp. 15-16; "Cocke v. Gooch" in Tenn. Rpts., 52:294; Bejach, 24-37)

BENTON

BENTON created from HUMPHREYS. (Tenn. Acts 1835, 21st assy., 1st sess., loc., ch. 30, secs. 1-2/p. 134)

BLOUNT (State of Franklin)

by Oct 1785
BLOUNT (State of Franklin) created from GREENE, probably at the Second General Assembly of Franklin in August 1785. The text of the act is not extant and the precise boundaries are unknown. It is not clear whether BLOUNT ever became fully organized; it is not to be confused with Tennessee's BLOUNT County created in 1795 in the same general area [not mapped]. (Williams, Samuel C., Lost State of Franklin, 88-89)
01 Feb 1789
BLOUNT eliminated with all other counties in the State of Franklin when John Sevier, governor of the State of Franklin, formally swore allegiance to North Carolina, effectively ending Franklin's operation and signaling the region's return to North Carolina control. (Folmsbee, Corlew, and Mitchell, 88-90; Williams, Samuel Cole, Lost State of Franklin, 213-225)

BLOUNT

02 Aug 1795
BLOUNT created by Territory of the United States South of the River Ohio (Southwest Territory) from KNOX and Non-County Area 1 (Cherokee Reserve). (Terr. South of R. Ohio Acts 1795, ch. 6/p. 60)
20 Apr 1796
Boundary between BLOUNT and SEVIER clarified [no change]. (Tenn. Acts 1796, 1st assy., 1st sess., ch. 35/p. 106)
01 Jun 1796
BLOUNT became a county in the newly-established state of Tennessee. (U.S. Stat., vol. 1, ch. 47[1796], pp. 491-492; Folmsbee, Corlew, and Mitchell 110)
28 Dec 1798
BLOUNT gained from Non-County Area 1 (Cherokee Reserve). (Tenn. Acts 1798, 2d assy., 2d sess., ch. 6/p. 165)
29 Oct 1801
BLOUNT gained all of Non-County Area 1 (Cherokee Reserve); Non-County Area 1 eliminated. (Tenn. Acts 1801, 4th assy., ch. 52/p. 289)

BLOUNT lost small area to SEVIER [change too small to display on interactive map; shapefile users see small_changes 1809_pt. for location]. (Scott, ch. 91/p. 1184)

BLOUNT lost to RHEA and ROANE. (Tenn. Acts 1815, 11th assy., ch. 200/p. 265)

BLOUNT gained from Non-County Area 9; Non-County Area 9 eliminated. (Tenn. Acts 1823, 15th assy., 1st sess., ch. 256, sec. 1/p. 218)

BLOUNT exchanged with MONROE. (Tenn. Acts 1835, 21st assy., 1st sess., loc., ch. 143/p. 269)

BLOUNT gained small area from MONROE. (Tenn. Acts 1837, 22d assy., ch. 270/p. 400)

CASWELL (State of Franklin)

01 Mar 1785
The First General Assembly of the State of Franklin convened in Jonesborough, Tenn., and recognized the three existing North Carolina counties located in eastern Tennessee (GREENE, SULLIVAN, and WASHINGTON) and created four new counties; the text of the acts is not extant and the precise boundaries of the counties are unknown. North Carolina did not recognize the legitimacy of these counties and sought to regain control of the area. CASWELL (State of Franklin) created from part of GREENE in the vicinity of present JEFFERSON and HAMBLEN [not mapped]. (Jordan, "Evolution . . . Hawkins and Sumner," 4-5, 8; Ramsey, 293-295; Williams, Samuel C., Lost State of Franklin, 55-58)
01 Feb 1789
CASWELL eliminated with all other counties in the State of Franklin when John Sevier, governor of the State of Franklin, formally swore allegiance to North Carolina, effectively ending Franklin's operation and signaling the region's return to North Carolina control. (Folmsbee, Corlew, and Mitchell, 88-90; Williams, Samuel Cole, Lost State of Franklin, 213-225)

CHEATHAM

05 Apr 1856
CHEATHAM created from DAVIDSON, MONTGOMERY, and ROBERTSON. CHEATHAM was located in the same general area where previous attempts had been made to create a CUMBERLAND County in 1837 and 1844. Part of DICKSON was to be included in CHEATHAM, but original plat excluded DICKSON due to constitutional considerations. (Tenn. Acts 1855, 31st assy., ch. 122, secs. 1, 18-21, 26/pp. 151, 156-158; "Davidson County v. Cheatham County" in S.W. Rptr, 63:209-213; Binkley, 30-31)

COCKE

09 Oct 1797
COCKE created from GREENE and JEFFERSON; part of JEFFERSON south of COCKE was left separate from the rest of JEFFERSON by this creation. (Tenn. Acts 1797, 2d assy., 1st sess., ch. 8, sec. 1/p. 124)
02 Jan 1799
COCKE gained from GREENE. (Tenn. Acts 1798, 2d assy., 2d sess., ch. 13/p. 168)
22 Oct 1811
COCKE lost small area to JEFFERSON. (Tenn. Acts 1811, 9th assy., 1st sess., ch. 41/p. 49)
19 Nov 1811
COCKE gained that part of JEFFERSON south of COCKE and east of SEVIER [see 9 October 1797]. (Tenn. Acts 1811, 9th assy., 1st sess., ch. 110/p. 128)
11 Oct 1817
COCKE exchanged with JEFFERSON to accommodate local residents [locations unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1817, 12th assy., ch. 23/p. 26)
11 Dec 1827
COCKE gained small area from JEFFERSON. (Tenn. Acts 1827, 17th assy., priv., ch. 176/p. 151)
28 Jan 1846
Legislature authorized COCKE to be renamed UNION; did not take effect [no change]. (Tenn. Acts 1845, 26th assy., ch. 123, sec. 10/p. 196)
04 Feb 1848
COCKE gained from GREENE to accommodate local resident [location unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1847, 27th assy., ch. 145/p. 226)
10 Mar 1879
COCKE gained from JEFFERSON to accommodate local resident [location unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1879, 41st assy., 1st sess., ch. 55/p. 75)
26 Mar 1883
COCKE gained from HAMBLEN to accommodate local residents [locations unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1883, 43d assy., ch. 118/p. 164)
27 Mar 1883
COCKE gained from JEFFERSON to accommodate local resident [location unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1883, 43d assy., ch. 139/p. 188)

COFFEE

08 Jan 1836
COFFEE created from BEDFORD, FRANKLIN, and WARREN. (Tenn. Acts 1835, 21st assy., 1st sess., loc., ch. 36, secs. 1, 14/pp. 155, 159)
04 Feb 1836
COFFEE gained from RUTHERFORD. Boundary between COFFEE and BEDFORD clarified [no change]. (Tenn. Acts 1835, 21st assy., 1st sess., loc., ch. 41/p. 168)
10 Feb 1838
COFFEE gained from FRANKLIN. (Tenn. Acts 1837, 22d assy., ch. 67, secs. 2, 4/p. 92)
27 May 1844
COFFEE lost to creation of GRUNDY. (Tenn. Acts 1843, 25th assy., ch. 204, secs. 1-2, 4/pp. 230-231; Nicholson, 18)
30 Jan 1846
COFFEE lost to GRUNDY [overturned by Tennessee Supreme Court, December 1848]. (Tenn. Acts 1845, 26th assy., ch. 134/p. 211)
01 Dec 1848
COFFEE gained from GRUNDY when Tennessee Supreme Court ruled act of 30 January 1846 unconstitutional and void. ("Gotcher v. Burrows" in Tenn. Rpts., 28:585-591 [Humphreys, vol. 9])
02 Feb 1850
COFFEE gained from GRUNDY to accommodate local resident [location unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1849, 28th assy., ch. 79/p. 260)
02 Feb 1852
COFFEE gained from GRUNDY to accommodate local residents [repealed 3 March 1854; location unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1851, 29th assy., ch. 262/p. 429)

COFFEE lost to GRUNDY to accommodate local residents [repealed act of 2 February 1852; locations unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1853, 30th assy., ch. 181/p. 250)

CROCKETT (proposed)

20 Dec 1845
Legislature authorized creation of CROCKETT from DYER, GIBSON, HAYWOOD, and MADISON. In October 1846, Circuit Court Judge in MADISON decreed CROCKETT's creation unconstitutional; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1845, 26th assy., ch. 25, secs. 1-2, 4/pp. 66-67; Goodspeed [F], 832; HRS Tenn., Crockett, 3-4)
24 Feb 1852
Legislature again authorized creation of CROCKETT from DYER, GIBSON, HAYWOOD, and MADISON; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1851, 29th assy., ch. 219, sec. 1/p. 327; ch. 195, secs. 1-2, 14/pp. 288, 292 and no. 17/p. 730; HRS Tenn., Crockett, 4; McBride, 8)
25 Jan 1866
Legislature again authorized creation of CROCKETT from DYER, GIBSON, HAYWOOD, and MADISON; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1865, 34th assy., 2d sess., pub., ch. 19, secs. 2-3/p. 25; HRS Tenn., Crockett, 4)
07 Jul 1870
Legislature again authorized creation of CROCKETT from DYER, GIBSON, HAYWOOD, and MADISON; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1870, 36th assy., 2d sess., ch. 89, secs. 1-2, 4/pp. 138-139; Tenn. Acts 1870, 36th assy., 3d sess., ch. 26/p. 31; HRS Tenn., Crockett, 4-5)

CROCKETT

19 Feb 1872
CROCKETT created from DYER, GIBSON, HAYWOOD, and MADISON. (Tenn. Acts 1871, 37th assy., 1st sess., ch. 132, secs. 1-2, 4/pp. 148-150; HRS Tenn., Crockett, 5-6)

CROCKETT gained from GIBSON to accommodate local residents [locations unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1879, 41st assy., 1st sess., ch. 137, secs. 1-17/pp. 174-177)

CUMBERLAND (proposed)

27 Nov 1837
Legislature authorized creation of a county named CUMBERLAND from DAVIDSON, DICKSON, MONTGOMERY, and ROBERTSON; creation did not take effect; not related to present CUMBERLAND. (Tenn. Acts 1837, 22d assy., ch. 8, secs. 1, 18, 20/pp. 28, 32-33 and ch. 124, secs. 1-3/pp. 189-190; McBride, 6-7; HRS Tenn., Cheatham, 5)
03 Jan 1844
Legislature again authorized creation of a county named CUMBERLAND from DAVIDSON, DICKSON, MONTGOMERY, and ROBERTSON; creation did not take effect; not related to present CUMBERLAND. CHEATHAM was created in this same general area in 1856. (Tenn. Acts 1843, 25th assy., ch. 59, secs. 1, 18, 20/pp. 59, 64-65; Tenn. Acts 1855, 31st assy., ch. 122, sec. 21/p. 157; McBride, 7; HRS Tenn., Cheatham, 5-6)

CUMBERLAND

16 Nov 1855
CUMBERLAND created from BLEDSOE, FENTRESS, MORGAN, PUTNAM, RHEA, and WHITE; not to be confused with the CUMBERLAND County which was proposed in 1837 and 1844 in a different part of the state. (Tenn. Acts 1855, 31st assy., ch. 6, sec. 1/p. 9)
29 Feb 1856
CUMBERLAND gained from MORGAN, RHEA, and ROANE. (Tenn. Acts 1855, 31st assy., ch. 166 [printed as 156]/p. 258)
17 Feb 1858
CUMBERLAND lost to FENTRESS. (Tenn. Acts 1857, 32d assy., pub., ch. 36/p. 44)
20 Mar 1858
CUMBERLAND lost to BLEDSOE to accommodate local residents [change too small to display on interactive map; shapefile users see small_changes 1858_pt. for location]. (Tenn. Acts 1857, 32d assy., pub., ch. 83, secs. 1-4, 8-9/pp. 91-93)
24 Mar 1860
CUMBERLAND gained from WHITE to accommodate local resident [location unknown, not mapped]; CUMBERLAND lost to RHEA to accommodate local resident [location unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1859, 33d assy., 1st sess., priv., ch. 210/p. 596)
15 Dec 1871
CUMBERLAND lost to PUTNAM to accommodate local resident [location unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1871, 37th assy., 1st sess., ch. 104/p. 117)
24 Mar 1873
CUMBERLAND lost to ROANE. (Tenn. Acts 1873, 38th assy., ch. 76/p. 110)
25 Mar 1879
CUMBERLAND lost to BLEDSOE to accommodate local residents [description clarified 14 March 1883; change too small to display on interactive map; shapefile users see small_changes 1879_pt. for location]. CUMBERLAND lost to ROANE to accommodate local resident [location unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1879, 41st assy., 1st sess., ch. 137, secs. 1-17/pp. 174-177)
09 Mar 1883
CUMBERLAND lost to WHITE to accommodate local resident [location unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1883, 43d assy., ch. 45/p. 49)

Boundary between CUMBERLAND and BLEDSOE clarified [corrected act of 25 March 1879; no change]. (Tenn. Acts 1883, 43d assy., ch. 58/p. 59)

DAVIDSON

17 May 1783
DAVIDSON created by North Carolina from WASHINGTON. (N.C. St. Recs., 24:ch. 52/p. 540)
06 Jan 1787
DAVIDSON lost to creation of SUMNER. (N.C. St. Recs., 24:ch. 32/pp. 826-828)
06 Dec 1788
DAVIDSON lost to creation of TENNESSEE County (extinct). (N.C. St. Recs., 24:ch. 28/pp. 972-973)
26 May 1790
The United States created the Territory of the United States South of the River Ohio (Southwest Territory), covering the territory ceded in April 1790 by North Carolina (area of present Tennessee). DAVIDSON became a county in the Southwest Territory. (Terr. Papers U.S., 4:18-19; U.S. Stat., vol. 1, ch. 14[1790], p. 123)
01 Jun 1796
DAVIDSON became a county in the newly-established state of Tennessee. (U.S. Stat., vol. 1, ch. 47[1796], pp. 491-492; Folmsbee, Corlew, and Mitchell 110)
29 Dec 1798
DAVIDSON gained from Non-County Area 2. (Tenn. Acts 1798, 2d assy., 2d sess., ch. 10/p. 167)
26 Oct 1799
DAVIDSON lost to creation of WILLIAMSON. (Tenn. Acts 1799, 3d assy., ch. 3, sec. 1/p. 182)
06 Nov 1801
DAVIDSON gained from WILSON. (Tenn. Acts 1801, 4th assy., ch. 57/p. 291)
14 Nov 1801
DAVIDSON gained from Non-County Area 2. (Tenn. Acts 1801, 4th assy., ch. 37/p. 270)
25 Oct 1803
DAVIDSON lost to creation of RUTHERFORD and lost to WILSON. (Tenn. Acts 1803, 5th assy., 1st sess., ch. 70/p. 119; ch. 74/p. 127)
02 Nov 1815
Legislature authorized WILLIAMSON to gain from DAVIDSON, dependent on local referendum [local action unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1815, 11th assy., ch. 153/p. 192)
27 Nov 1837
Legislature authorized creation of a county named CUMBERLAND from DAVIDSON and three other counties; creation did not take effect; not related to present CUMBERLAND. (Tenn. Acts 1837, 22d assy., ch. 8, secs. 1, 18, 20/pp. 28, 32-33 and ch. 124, secs. 1-3/pp. 189-190; McBride, 6-7; HRS Tenn., Cheatham, 5)
03 Jan 1844
Legislature again authorized creation of a county named CUMBERLAND from DAVIDSON and three other counties; creation did not take effect; not related to present CUMBERLAND. (Tenn. Acts 1843, 25th assy., ch. 59, secs. 1, 18, 20/pp. 59, 64-65; Tenn. Acts 1855, 31st assy., ch. 122, sec. 21/p. 157; McBride, 7; HRS Tenn., Cheatham, 5-6)
01 May 1848
DAVIDSON gained from RUTHERFORD. (Tenn. Acts 1847, 27th assy., ch. 145/p. 226)

ETHERIDGE (proposed)

06 Jun 1870
Legislature authorized creation of ETHERIDGE from CARROLL, GIBSON, HENDERSON, MADISON, and WEAKLEY; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1870, 36th assy., 2d sess., ch. 3, secs. 1-2, 4-7/pp. 9-12; McBride, 8)

FAYETTE

29 Sep 1824
FAYETTE created from Non-County Area 13 attached to HARDEMAN; Non-County Area 13 eliminated ending its attachment to HARDEMAN. (Tenn. Acts 1824, 15th assy., 2d sess., ch. 36, sec. 1/p. 46)
16 Jan 1844
Legislature authorized creation of HANOVER from FAYETTE and SHELBY; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1843, 25th assy., ch. 123, secs. 1, 5, 10/pp. 153-156; McBride, 8)
20 Dec 1870
Legislature authorized creation of BELL from FAYETTE, HARDEMAN, and McNAIRY; voided by Tennessee Supreme Court, 8 June 1871. (Tenn. Acts 1870, 36th assy., 3d sess., ch. 16, secs. 1-2,4/pp. 15-16; "Cocke v. Gooch" in Tenn. Rpts., 52:294; Bejach, 24-37)
04 Nov 1871
Legislature authorized creation of NASHOBA from FAYETTE and SHELBY; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1871, 37th assy., 1st sess., ch. 16, secs. 1-2, 4, 12/pp. 14-17 and ch. 82/p. 73; McBride, 8)
18 Mar 1883
FAYETTE lost small area to TIPTON. (Tenn. Acts 1883, 43d assy., ch. 81/p. 75)
28 Mar 1883
FAYETTE lost to HARDEMAN to accommodate local residents [locations unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1883, 43d assy., ch. 125/p. 171)
13 Apr 1907
FAYETTE gained from HARDEMAN to accommodate local resident [location unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1907, 55th assy., ch. 429/p. 1459)

FENTRESS

28 Nov 1823
FENTRESS created from CAMPBELL, MORGAN, and OVERTON. (Tenn. Acts 1823, 15th assy., 1st sess., ch. 302, secs. 1-2/p. 260)
16 Dec 1831
FENTRESS lost to OVERTON to accommodate local resident [change too small to display on interactive map; shapefile users see small_changes 1831_pt. for location]. (Tenn. Acts 1831, 19th assy., stated sess., priv., ch. 153/p. 125)
02 Feb 1842
FENTRESS lost to creation of PUTNAM. (Tenn. Acts 1841, 24th assy., 1st sess., ch. 169, sec. 1/p. 186)
in Mar 1845
FENTRESS gained part of PUTNAM; PUTNAM eliminated when OVERTON Chancery Court declared PUTNAM to have been unconstitutionally established. (DeLozier, 21; McBride, 11; Tenn. Acts 1845, 26th assy., ch. 75/p. 141)
02 Feb 1846
FENTRESS exchanged with MORGAN. (Tenn. Acts 1845, 26th assy., ch. 175/p. 260)
17 Dec 1849
FENTRESS lost to creation of SCOTT. (Tenn. Acts 1849, 28th assy., ch. 45, secs. 1-2, 4/pp. 145, 147)

GIBSON

21 Oct 1823
GIBSON created from all of Non-County Area 10 attached to CARROLL; Non-County Area 10 eliminated. (Tenn. Acts 1823, 15th assy., 1st sess., ch. 111/p. 116)
13 Nov 1823
GIBSON boundaries clarified [no change]. (Tenn. Acts 1823, 15th assy., 1st sess., ch. 206/p. 184)
04 Nov 1837
GIBSON exchanged with WEAKLEY. (Tenn. Acts 1837, 22d assy., ch. 245/p. 365)
20 Dec 1845
Legislature authorized creation of CROCKETT from GIBSON and three other counties; in October 1846 Circuit Court Judge in MADISON decreed CROCKETT's creation unconstitutional; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1845, 26th assy., ch. 25, secs. 1-2, 4/pp. 66-67; Goodspeed [F], 832; HRS Tenn., Crockett, 3-4)
01 Feb 1850
GIBSON gained from DYER. (Tenn. Acts 1849, 28th assy., ch. 83/p. 268)
24 Feb 1852
Legislature authorized creation of CHRISTIAN from GIBSON and three other counties; creation did not take effect. Legislature again authorized creation of CROCKETT from GIBSON and three other counties; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1851, 29th assy., ch. 219, sec. 1/p. 327; ch. 195, secs. 1-2, 14/pp. 288, 292 and no. 17/p. 730; HRS Tenn., Crockett, 4; McBride, 8)
25 Jan 1866
Legislature again authorized creation of CROCKETT from GIBSON and three other counties; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1865, 34th assy., 2d sess., pub., ch. 19, secs. 2-3/p. 25; HRS Tenn., Crockett, 4)
25 Feb 1869
Legislature authorized creation of GRANT from GIBSON and three other counties; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1868, 35th assy., 2d sess., pub., ch. 39, secs. 1-3, 5, 15/pp. 53-54, 56; McBride, 8)
06 Jun 1870
Legislature authorized creation of ETHERIDGE from GIBSON and four other counties; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1870, 36th assy., 2d sess., ch. 3, secs. 1-2, 4-7/pp. 9-12; McBride, 8)
07 Jul 1870
Legislature again authorized creation of CROCKETT from GIBSON and three other counties; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1870, 36th assy., 2d sess., ch. 89, secs. 1-2, 4/pp. 138-139; Tenn. Acts 1870, 36th assy., 3d sess., ch. 26/p. 31; HRS Tenn., Crockett, 4-5)
19 Feb 1872

GRANT (proposed)

25 Feb 1869
Legislature authorized creation of GRANT from CARROLL, GIBSON, HENDERSON, and MADISON; creation did not take effect. GRANT was to be in the same general area as CHRISTIAN, which was proposed in 1852 but never organized. (Tenn. Acts 1868, 35th assy., 2d sess., pub., ch. 39, secs. 1-3, 5, 15/pp. 53-54, 56; McBride, 8)

GREENE

17 May 1783
GREENE created by North Carolina from WASHINGTON; precise location of boundary between North Carolina and Virginia remained in dispute. (N.C. St. Recs., 24:ch. 51/pp. 539-540 and ch. 2, sec. 5/p. 479)
01 Mar 1785
GREENE lost to creation of three counties in the state of FRANKLIN: CASWELL, SEVIER, and SPENCER; North Carolina did not recognize the legitimacy of these counties and precise boundaries are unknown [not mapped]. (Jordan, "Evolution . . . Hawkins and Sumner," 4-5, 8; Ramsey, 293-295; Williams, Samuel C., Lost State of Franklin, 55-58)
01 Oct 1785
GREENE lost to creation of BLOUNT (State of Franklin); North Carolina did not recognize the legitimacy of BLOUNT and precise boundaries are unknown [not mapped]. (Williams, Samuel C., Lost State of Franklin, 88-89)
06 Jan 1787
GREENE lost to creation of HAWKINS, lost to creation of Non-County Area 1 (Cherokee Reserve), and Non-County Area 2 when territory east and west of HAWKINS implicitly reverted to non-county status. (N.C. St. Recs., 24:ch. 34/pp. 830-832)
26 May 1790
The United States created the Territory of the United States South of the River Ohio (Southwest Territory), covering the territory ceded in April by North Carolina (area of present Tennessee and a small area of North Carolina). GREENE became a county in the Southwest Territory. (Terr. Papers U.S., 4:18-19; U.S. Stat., vol. 1, ch. 14[1790], p. 123)
15 Jun 1792
GREENE lost to creation of JEFFERSON and KNOX. (Terr. Papers U.S., 4:448-449)
07 May 1793
GREENE exchanged with JEFFERSON. (Terr. Papers U.S., 4:455-456)
01 Jun 1796
GREENE became a county in the newly-established state of Tennessee. (U.S. Stat., vol. 1, ch. 47[1796], pp. 491-492; Folmsbee, Corlew, and Mitchell 110)
09 Oct 1797
GREENE lost to creation of COCKE. (Tenn. Acts 1797, 2d assy., 1st sess., ch. 8, sec. 1/p. 124)
02 Jan 1799
GREENE lost to COCKE. (Tenn. Acts 1798, 2d assy., 2d sess., ch. 13/p. 168)
11 Sep 1806
GREENE lost to HAWKINS. (Scott, ch. 53/p. 975)
c. Dec 1835
Legislature authorized creation of POWELL from GREENE and three other counties, dependent on local referendum; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1835, 21st assy., 1st sess., loc., ch. 29, secs. 1-3/pp. 129-130)
c. Jan 1838
Legislature again authorized creation of POWELL from GREENE and three other counties; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1837, 22d assy., ch. 192, secs. 1-3, 15-16/pp. 277, 280-281 and ch. 199, sec. 4/p. 291)
c. Nov 1839
Legislature again authorized creation of POWELL from GREENE and three other counties; this creation was disallowed by the Tennessee Supreme Court in 1841. (Tenn. Acts 1839, 23d assy., ch. 15, secs. 1-2, 4-5, 16/pp. 25-27, 30; "Bradley v. Commissioners" in Tenn. Rpts., 21:428-433 [Humphreys, vol. 2])
04 Feb 1848
GREENE lost to COCKE to accommodate local resident [location unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1847, 27th assy., ch. 145/p. 226)
02 Mar 1854
Legislature again authorized creation of POWELL from GREENE and three other counties; creation did not take effect. It is unclear whether any of WASHINGTON was actually included within the boundaries as described. (Tenn. Acts 1853, 30th assy., ch. 89, secs. 1-3, 8, 10, 14/pp. 158-163)
07 Dec 1869
Legislature again authorized creation of POWELL from GREENE and three other counties; creation did not take effect; boundary description was identical to that proposed in 1854. (Tenn. Acts 1869, 36th assy., 1st sess., pub., ch. 30, secs. 1-2, 4, 11-12, 19-20/pp. 33-38; McBride, 9)
05 Apr 1881
GREENE gained from UNICOI and WASHINGTON. (Tenn. Acts 1881, 42d assy., 1st sess., ch. 145/p. 194)
18 Mar 1891
GREENE lost to WASHINGTON to accommodate local residents [locations unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1891, 47th assy., ch. 142/p. 313)
14 May 1895
GREENE lost to WASHINGTON to accommodate local resident. (Tenn. Acts 1895, 49th assy., ch. 176/p. 375)
28 Feb 1972
GREENE gained from WASHINGTON to accommodate local resident. (Tenn. Acts 1972, 87th assy., 2d reg. sess., pub., ch. 450/p. 19)
13 Apr 1973
GREENE gained from WASHINGTON to accommodate local resident [location unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1973, 88th assy., 1st reg. sess., pub., ch. 79, sec. 1/p. 186)
19 Apr 1973
GREENE lost to WASHINGTON to accommodate local residents [locations unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1973, 88th assy., 1st reg. sess., pub., ch. 102, sec. 1/p. 274)
17 Apr 1980
GREENE lost small areas to WASHINGTON [locations unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1980, 91st assy., 2d reg. sess., pub., ch. 795, sec. 1/p. 918)
22 Apr 1982
GREENE lost to WASHINGTON to accommodate local resident [location unknown not mapped; map depicts net changes in GREENE-WASHINGTON line 1891-1982]. (Tenn. Acts 1982, 92d assy., 2d reg. sess., pub., ch. 855/p. 514)

HAWKINS

06 Jan 1787
HAWKINS created by North Carolina from GREENE and SULLIVAN. Precise boundary between North Carolina and Virginia remained in dispute. (N.C. St. Recs., 24:ch. 34/pp. 830-832)
26 May 1790
The United States created the Territory of the United States South of the River Ohio (Southwest Territory), covering the territory ceded in April by North Carolina (area of present Tennessee). HAWKINS became a county in the Southwest Territory. (Terr. Papers U.S., 4:18-19; U.S. Stat., vol. 1, ch. 14[1790], p. 123)
15 Jun 1792
HAWKINS lost to creation of JEFFERSON and KNOX. (Terr. Papers U.S., 4:448-449)
22 Apr 1796
HAWKINS lost to creation of GRAINGER; all that part of HAWKINS south of GRAINGER implicitly reverted to non-county area status, and became part of Non-County Area 2. (Tenn. Acts 1796, 1st assy., 1st sess., ch. 28, sec. 1/p. 95)
01 Jun 1796
HAWKINS became a county in the newly-established state of Tennessee. (U.S. Stat., vol. 1, ch. 47[1796], pp. 491-492; Folmsbee, Corlew, and Mitchell 110)
28 Oct 1797
HAWKINS lost to GRAINGER. (Tenn. Acts 1797, 2d assy., 1st sess., ch. 13/p. 129)
05 Jan 1799
HAWKINS gained from GRAINGER. (Tenn. Acts 1798, 2d assy., 2d sess., ch. 21/p. 172)
06 Dec 1801
HAWKINS lost to creation of CLAIBORNE. (Tenn. Acts 1801, 4th assy., ch. 46, secs. 1, 13, 17/pp. 279, 281)
11 Sep 1806
HAWKINS gained from GREENE. (Scott, ch. 53/p. 975)

HAWKINS lost small area to GRAINGER [change too small to display on interactive map; shapefile users see small_changes 1809_pt. for location]. (Scott, ch. 29/p. 1136)
16 Oct 1815
Boundary between HAWKINS and JEFFERSON adjusted to accommodate local resident [change too small to display on interactive map; shapefile users see small_changes 1815_pt. for location]. (Tenn. Acts 1815, 11th assy., ch. 13/p. 14)

c. Dec 1835

c. Jan 1838
Legislature again authorized creation of POWELL from HAWKINS and three other counties; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1837, 22d assy., ch. 192, secs. 1-3, 15-16/pp. 277, 280-281 and ch. 199, sec. 4/p. 291)
c. Nov 1839

Acts 1839, 23d assy., ch. 15, secs. 1-2, 4-5, 16/pp. 25-27, 30; "Bradley v. Commissioners" in Tenn. Rpts., 21:428-433 [Humphreys, vol. 2])

29 Jan 1846

MONTGOMERY lost to creation of STEWART, lost to Non-County Area 3 when a one-mile-wide strip of MONTGOMERY between STEWART and DICKSON implicitly reverted to non-county status, and lost to Non-County Area 4 when territory west of Tennessee River implicitly reverted to non-county status (Chickasaw Indian land). (Tenn. Acts 1803, 5th assy., 1st sess., ch. 68, sec. 1/p. 115)

MONTGOMERY exchanged with STEWART. (Scott, ch. 13/p. 830)

NASHOBA (proposed)

04 Nov 1871
Legislature authorized creation of NASHOBA from FAYETTE and SHELBY; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1871, 37th assy., 1st sess., ch. 16, secs. 1-2, 4, 12/pp. 14-17 and ch. 82/p. 73; McBride, 8)

Non-County Area 1

06 Jan 1787
Non-County Area 1 (Cherokee Reserve) implicitly created when GREENE lost to creation of HAWKINS. (N.C. St. Recs., 24:ch. 34/pp. 830-832)
15 Jun 1792
Non-County Area 1 (Cherokee Reserve) lost to creation of JEFFERSON and KNOX. (Terr. Papers U.S., 4:448-449)
27 Sep 1794
Non-County Area 1 (Cherokee Reserve) gained from JEFFERSON. (Terr. South of R. Ohio Acts 1794, ch. 11/p. 38)
02 Aug 1795
Non-County Area 1 (Cherokee Reserve) lost to BLOUNT. (Terr. South of R. Ohio Acts 1795, ch. 6/p. 60)
28 Dec 1798
Non-County Area 1 (Cherokee Reserve) lost to BLOUNT. (Tenn. Acts 1798, 2d assy., 2d sess., ch. 6/p. 165)
29 Oct 1801
Non-County Area 1 (Cherokee Reserve) eliminated when it lost all territory to BLOUNT. (Tenn. Acts 1801, 4th assy., ch. 52/p. 289)

Non-County Area 2

06 Jan 1787
Non-County Area 2 created when that part of GREENE west of HAWKINS reverted to non-county status. (N.C. St. Recs., 24:ch. 34/pp. 830-832)
22 Apr 1796
Non-County Area 2 gained when all that part of HAWKINS south of GRAINGER implicitly reverted to non-county status. (Tenn. Acts 1796, 1st assy., 1st sess., ch. 28, sec. 1/p. 95)
29 Dec 1798
Non-County Area 2 lost to DAVIDSON and exchanged with SUMNER when that part of SUMNER east of Indian boundary reverted to non-county status. (Tenn. Acts 1798, 2d assy., 2d sess., ch. 10/p. 167)
05 Jan 1799
Non-County Area 2 exchanged with GRAINGER . (Tenn. Acts 1798, 2d assy., 2d sess., ch. 21/p. 172)
10 Jan 1799
Non-County Area 2 lost to KNOX. (Tenn. Acts 1798, 2d assy., 2d sess., ch. 22/p. 172)
29 Oct 1801
Non-County Area 2 gained when parts of MONTGOMERY and ROBERTSON reverted to non-county status. (Tenn. Acts 1801, 4th assy., ch. 51/p. 289)
14 Nov 1801
Non-County Area 2 lost to DAVIDSON, JACKSON, MONTGOMERY, ROBERTSON, SMITH, WILLIAMSON, and WILSON. (Tenn. Acts 1801, 4th assy., ch. 37/p. 270)
06 Dec 1801
Non-County Area 2 lost to creation of CLAIBORNE. (Tenn. Acts 1801, 4th assy., ch. 46, secs. 1, 13, 17/pp. 279, 281)
13 Dec 1801
Non-County Area 2 lost to creation of ANDERSON. (Tenn. Acts 1801, 4th assy., ch. 45, secs. 1, 2, 4, 30/pp. 274, 279)
20 Dec 1801
Non-County Area 2 eliminated when in lost all territory to creation of ROANE. (Tenn. Acts 1801, 4th assy., ch. 45, secs. 1, 3, 4, 30/pp. 274, 279)

Non-County Area 3

01 Nov 1803
Non-County Area 3 created when a one-mile strip of MONTGOMERY, between STEWART and DICKSON, implicitly reverted to non-county status. (Tenn. Acts 1807, 7th assy., 1st sess., ch. 44/p. 79)
31 Jul 1804
Non-County Area 3 lost to STEWART. (Scott, ch. 13/p. 830)
01 Jan 1808
Non-County Area 3 lost to creation of HICKMAN. (Tenn. Acts 1807, 7th assy., 1st sess., ch. 44/p. 79)
19 Oct 1809
Non-County Area 3 eliminated when it lost all territory to creation of HUMPHREYS. (Scott, ch. 31/p. 1138)

Non-County Area 4

01 Nov 1803
Non-County Area 4 created when territory west of Tennessee River implicitly reverted to non-county status (Chickasaw Indian land). (Tenn. Acts 1803, 5th assy., 1st sess., ch. 68, sec. 1/p. 115)
19 Oct 1809
Non-County Area 4 gained when that part of STEWART south of HUMPHREYS reverted to non-county status. (Scott, ch. 31/p. 1138)
24 Nov 1817
Non-County Area 4 lost to creation of WAYNE; act was technically not valid, but citizens proceeded with the organization of the county. (Tenn. Acts 1817, 12th assy., ch. 174, sec. 1/p. 209)
08 Oct 1819
Non-County Area 4 gained when part of WAYNE reverted to non-county area that became part of HARDIN on 13 November 1819. (Tenn. Acts 1819, 13th assy., 1st sess., loc.-priv., ch. 19, secs. 1, 4-6/pp. 24-26)
13 Nov 1819
Non-County Area 4 lost to creation of HARDIN. (Tenn. Acts 1819, 13th assy., 1st sess., pub., ch. 6/p. 33)
15 Nov 1819
Non-County Area 4 lost to HUMPHREYS. (Tenn. Acts 1819, 13th assy., 1st sess., pub., ch. 2/p. 28)
18 Nov 1819
Non-County Area 4 lost to creation of PERRY; western limit of PERRY not explicitly defined until 14 November 1821. (Tenn. Acts 1819, 13th assy., 1st sess., loc.-priv., ch. 107, sec. 1/p. 132)
26 Jul 1820
Non-County Area 4 lost to HUMPHREYS. (Tenn. Acts 1820, 13th assy., 2d sess., loc.-priv., ch. 90/p. 86)
07 Nov 1821
Non-County Area 4 eliminated when it lost all territory to creation of CARROLL, HENDERSON, HENRY, MADISON, and Non-County Areas 10, 11, 12, and 13. (Tenn. Acts 1821, 14th assy., 1st sess., pub., ch. 32/pp. 39-44)

Non-County Area 5

28 Oct 1805
Non-County Area 5 created when those parts of SMITH and WILSON lying south of the Indian boundary reverted to non-county status. (Tenn. Acts 1805, 6th assy., 1st sess., ch. 67/p. 72)
11 Sep 1806
Non-County Area 5 eliminated when it lost all territory to creation of WHITE. (Scott, ch. 36/p. 963)

Non-County Area 6

26 Nov 1807
Non-County Area 6 created when eastern and southern portions of WHITE reverted to non-county status. (Tenn. Acts 1807, 7th assy., 1st sess., ch. 28/p. 62)
30 Nov 1807
Non-County Area 6 lost to creation of BLEDSOE. (Tenn. Acts 1807, 7th assy., 1st sess., ch. 9, secs. 1-3/p. 39)
03 Dec 1807
Non-County Area 6 eliminated when it lost all territory to creation of FRANKLIN. (Tenn. Acts 1807, 7th assy., 1st sess., ch. 72, sec. 1/p. 118)

Non-County Area 7

15 Dec 1807
Non-County Area 7 created when parts of DICKSON and WILLIAMSON south of MAURY reverted to non-county status. Non-County Area 7 attached to MAURY for administrative and judicial purposes. (Tenn. Acts 1807, 7th assy., 1st sess., ch. 94, secs. 1-2, 13, 16/pp. 149-153)
01 Jan 1810
Non-County Area 7 attached to MAURY lost to creation of GILES. (Scott, ch. 55/p. 1162)
21 Oct 1817
Non-County Area 7 eliminated when it lost all territory to creation of LAWRENCE. (Tenn. Acts 1817, 12th assy., ch. 42/p. 48)

Non-County Area 8

09 Oct 1817
Non-County Area 8 created when part of RHEA reverted to non-county status. (Tenn. Acts 1817, 12th assy., ch. 13/p. 15)
26 Dec 1817
Non-County Area 8 lost to creation of MARION. (Tenn. Acts 1817, 12th assy., ch. 109, sec. 1-2, 8/pp. 113-115; U.S. Stat., vol. 7, p. 156)
25 Oct 1819
Non-County Area 8 eliminated when it lost all territory to creation of HAMILTON. (Tenn. Acts 1819, 13th assy., 1st sess., loc.-priv., ch. 41/p. 55)

Non-County Area 9

13 Nov 1819
Non-County Area 9 created when part of ROANE reverted to non-county status. (Tenn. Acts 1819, 13th assy., 1st sess., pub., ch. 3/p. 29)
22 Nov 1823
Non-County Area 9 eliminated when it lost all territory to BLOUNT and MONROE. (Tenn. Acts 1823, 15th assy., 1st sess., ch. 256, sec. 1/p. 218)

Non-County Area 10

07 Nov 1821
Non-County Area 10 created from Non-County Area 4. Non-County Area 10 attached to CARROLL for administrative and judicial purposes. (Tenn. Acts 1821, 14th assy., 1st sess., pub., ch. 32/pp. 39-44)
23 Aug 1822
Non-County Area 10 lost when part of it was detached from CARROLL and became part of Non-County Area 12 attached to MADISON. (Tenn. Acts 1822, 14th assy., 2d sess., ch. 199/p. 157)
21 Oct 1823
Non-County Area 10 eliminated when it lost all territory to creation of GIBSON. (Tenn. Acts 1823, 15th assy., 1st sess., ch. 111/p. 116)

Non-County Area 11

07 Nov 1821
Non-County Area 11 created from Non-County Area 4. Non-County Area 11 attached to HENRY for administrative and judicial purposes. (Tenn. Acts 1821, 14th assy., 1st sess., pub., ch. 32/pp. 39-44)
21 Oct 1823
Non-County Area 11 lost to creation of WEAKLEY. (Tenn. Acts 1823, 15th assy., 1st sess., ch. 112/p. 117)
24 Oct 1823
Non-County Area 11 eliminated when it lost all territory to creation of OBION. (Tenn. Acts 1823, 15th assy., 1st sess., ch. 114/p. 119)

07 Nov 1821
Non-County Area 13 created from part of HARDIN that reverted to non-county status, and from Non-County Area 4. Non-County Area 13 attached to SHELBY for administrative and judicial purposes. (Tenn. Acts 1821, 14th assy., 1st sess., pub., ch. 32/pp. 39-44)

PICKETT

in Apr 1881
PICKETT created from FENTRESS and OVERTON. PICKETT's east line was supposed to run along the western limit of SCOTT as defined in 1849; it appears legislators ignored the 4 November 1871 change in SCOTT's west line. (Tenn. Acts 1879, 41st assy., 1st sess., ch. 34, secs. 1-2, 4/pp. 48-50; Tenn. Acts 1881, 42d assy., 1st sess., ch. 37, sec 1/p. 35; Huddleston, 37)

POWELL (proposed)

c. Dec 1835
Legislature authorized creation of POWELL from GREENE, HAWKINS, SULLIVAN, and WASHINGTON, dependent on local referendum; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1835, 21st assy., 1st sess., loc., ch. 29, secs. 1-3/pp. 129-130)
c. Jan 1838
Legislature again authorized creation of POWELL from GREENE, HAWKINS, SULLIVAN, and WASHINGTON; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1837, 22d assy., ch. 192, secs. 1-3, 15-16/pp. 277, 280-281 and ch. 199, sec. 4/p. 291)
c. Nov 1839
Legislature again authorized creation of POWELL from GREENE, HAWKINS, SULLIVAN, and WASHINGTON; this creation was disallowed by the Tennessee Supreme Court in 1841. (Tenn. Acts 1839, 23d assy., ch. 15, secs. 1-2, 4-5, 16/pp. 25-27, 30; "Bradley v. Commissioners" in Tenn. Rpts., 21:428-433 [Humphreys, vol. 2])
02 Mar 1854
Legislature again authorized creation of POWELL from GREENE, HAWKINS, SULLIVAN, and WASHINGTON; creation did not take effect. It is unclear whether any of WASHINGTON was actually included within the boundaries as described. (Tenn. Acts 1853, 30th assy., ch. 89, secs. 1-3, 8, 10, 14/pp. 158-163)
17 Mar 1858
Legislature authorized the organization of POWELL according to the provisions of the act passed 2 March 1854; did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1857, 32d assy., priv., ch. 143/p. 350)
07 Dec 1869
Legislature again authorized creation of POWELL from GREENE, HAWKINS, SULLIVAN, and WASHINGTON; creation did not take effect; boundary description was identical to that proposed in 1854. (Tenn. Acts 1869, 36th assy., 1st sess., pub., ch. 30, secs. 1-2, 4, 11-12, 19-20/pp. 33-38; McBride, 9)

PUTNAM

02 Feb 1842
PUTNAM created from FENTRESS, JACKSON, OVERTON, and WHITE. (Tenn. Acts 1841, 24th assy., 1st sess., ch. 169, sec. 1/p. 186)
in Mar 1845
PUTNAM eliminated when OVERTON Chancery Court declared PUTNAM to have been unconstitutionally established. (DeLozier, 21; McBride, 11; Tenn. Acts 1845, 26th assy., ch. 75/p. 141)
11 Feb 1854
PUTNAM re-created from DEKALB, FENTRESS, JACKSON, OVERTON, SMITH, and WHITE; boundaries were slightly different from 1842 county. (Tenn. Acts 1853, 30th assy., ch. 320, secs. 1-2, 10, 21, 24-25/pp. 744-754)

Acts 1915, 59th assy., priv., ch. 541/p. 1735; ch. 477/p. 1560; ch. 656/p. 2137)
in Dec 1917
Tennessee Supreme Court upheld act of 17 May 1915 (ch. 477) and ruled that the Ravenscroft area, which was transferred from PUTNAM to WHITE by said act, had actually always been part of WHITE, thus invalidating the 1902 boundary survey. Supreme Court also upheld ruling of PUTNAM Chancery Court which overturned act of 17 May 1915 (ch. 656). ("Putnam County v. White County" in Tenn. Rpts., 140:19-33)

SEVIER (State of Franklin)

01 Mar 1785
The First General Assembly of the State of Franklin convened in Jonesborough, Tenn., and recognized the three existing North Carolina counties located in eastern Tennessee (GREENE, SULLIVAN, and WASHINGTON) and created four new counties; the text of the acts is not extant and the precise boundaries of the counties are unknown. North Carolina did not recognize the legitimacy of these counties and sought to regain control of the area. SEVIER (State of Franklin) created from GREENE; it is not to be confused with Tennessee's SEVIER County created in 1794 in the same general area [not mapped]. (Jordan, "Evolution . . . Hawkins and Sumner," 4-5, 8; Ramsey, 293-295; Williams, Samuel C., Lost State of Franklin, 55-58)
01 Feb 1789
SEVIER eliminated with all other counties in the State of Franklin when John Sevier, governor of the State of Franklin, formally swore allegiance to North Carolina, effectively ending Franklin's operation and signaling the region's return to North Carolina control. (Folmsbee, Corlew, and Mitchell, 88-90; Williams, Samuel Cole, Lost State of Franklin, 213-225)

SMITH gained from PUTNAM to accommodate local resident [overturned by Tennessee Supreme Court, December 1913; change too small to display on interactive map; shapefile users see small_changes 1905_pt. for location]. (Tenn. Acts 1905, 54th assy., ch. 370/p. 776)

in Dec 1913

("Putnam County v. Smith County" in Tenn. Rpts., 129:394-397)

SPENCER (State of Franklin)

01 Mar 1785
The First General Assembly of the State of Franklin convened in Jonesborough, Tenn., and recognized the three existing North Carolina counties located in eastern Tennessee (GREENE, SULLIVAN, and WASHINGTON) and created four new counties; the text of the acts is not extant and the precise boundaries of the counties are unknown. North Carolina did not recognize the legitimacy of these counties and sought to regain control of the area. SPENCER (State of Franklin) created from GREENE and SULLIVAN in the vicinity of present HAWKINS [not mapped]. (Jordan, "Evolution . . . Hawkins and Sumner," 4-5, 8; Ramsey, 293-295; Williams, Samuel C., Lost State of Franklin, 55-58)
01 Feb 1789
SPENCER eliminated with all other counties in the State of Franklin when John Sevier, governor of the State of Franklin, formally swore allegiance to North Carolina, effectively ending Franklin's operation and signaling the region's return to North Carolina control. (Folmsbee, Corlew, and Mitchell, 88-90; Williams, Samuel Cole, Lost State of Franklin, 213-225)

STEWART

01 Nov 1803
STEWART created from MONTGOMERY. (Tenn. Acts 1803, 5th assy., 1st sess., ch. 68, sec. 1/p. 115)
31 Jul 1804
STEWART gained from DICKSON and Non-County Area 3; exchanged with MONTGOMERY. (Scott, ch. 13/p. 830)
19 Oct 1809
STEWART lost to creation of HUMPHREYS; that part of STEWART south of HUMPHREYS reverted to Non-County Area 4. (Scott, ch. 31/p. 1138)
26 Jul 1820
STEWART gained from HUMPHREYS. (Tenn. Acts 1821, 14th assy., 1st sess., loc.-priv., ch. 125/p. 128)
22 Nov 1823
STEWART lost to HUMPHREYS. (Tenn. Acts 1823, 15th assy., 1st sess., ch. 251/p. 215)
15 Feb 1840
STEWART lost to HUMPHREYS. (Tenn. Acts 1839, 23d assy., ch. 76/p. 158)
23 Feb 1871
STEWART lost to creation of HOUSTON. (Tenn. Acts 1870, 36th assy., 3d sess., ch. 46, secs. 1-2, 4, 18, 20/pp. 49-51, 55; McClain, Iris H., 1-2)
25 Feb 1909
STEWART gained from HOUSTON. (Tenn. Acts 1909, 56th assy., ch. 126, secs. 1-3/pp. 447-449)

SULLIVAN

10 Nov 1779
SULLIVAN created by North Carolina from WASHINGTON; western limit not defined. North Holston and Carters Valley settlements came under the control of SULLIVAN. Precise location of boundary between North Carolina and Virginia remained in dispute. (N.C. St. Recs., 24:ch. 29/pp. 300-302)
01 Mar 1785
SULLIVAN lost to creation of SPENCER (State of Franklin); North Carolina did not recognize the legitimacy of SPENCER and its precise boundaries are unknown [not mapped]. (Jordan, "Evolution . . . Hawkins and Sumner," 4-5, 8; Ramsey, 293-295; Williams, Samuel C., Lost State of Franklin, 55-58)
06 Jan 1787
SULLIVAN lost to creation of HAWKINS. (N.C. St. Recs., 24:ch. 34/pp. 830-832)
06 Dec 1788
SULLIVAN gained from WASHINGTON. (N.C. St. Recs., 24:ch. 29/p. 974)
26 May 1790
The United States created the Territory of the United States South of the River Ohio (Southwest Territory), covering the territory ceded in April by North Carolina (area of present Tennessee and a small area of North Carolina). SULLIVAN became a county in the Southwest Territory. (Terr. Papers U.S., 4:18-19; U.S. Stat., vol. 1, ch. 14[1790], p. 123)
01 Jun 1796
SULLIVAN became a county in the newly-established state of Tennessee. (U.S. Stat., vol. 1, ch. 47[1796], pp. 491-492; Folmsbee, Corlew, and Mitchell 110)
04 Aug 1804
SULLIVAN lost to CARTER. (Scott, ch. 18/pp. 833-834)
24 Oct 1805
Boundary between SULLIVAN and CARTER clarified [no change]. (Tenn. Acts 1805, 6th assy., 1st sess., ch. 46/p. 45)
c. Dec 1835
Legislature authorized creation of POWELL from SULLIVAN and three other counties; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1835, 21st assy., 1st sess., loc., ch. 29, secs. 1-3/pp. 129-130)
c. Jan 1838
Legislature again authorized creation of POWELL from SULLIVAN and three other counties; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1837, 22d assy., ch. 192, secs. 1-3, 15-16/pp. 277, 280-281 and ch. 199, sec. 4/p. 291)
c. Nov 1839
Legislature again authorized creation of POWELL from SULLIVAN and three other counties; this creation was disallowed by the Tennessee Supreme Court in 1841. (Tenn. Acts 1839, 23d assy., ch. 15, secs. 1-2, 4-5, 16/pp. 25-27, 30; "Bradley v. Commissioners" in Tenn. Rpts., 21:428-433 [Humphreys, vol. 2])
02 Jan 1846
SULLIVAN exchanged with WASHINGTON to accommodate local residents [location of WASHINGTON gain unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1845, 26th assy., ch. 47/p. 101)
02 Mar 1854
Legislature again authorized creation of POWELL from SULLIVAN and three other counties; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1853, 30th assy., ch. 89, secs. 1-3, 8, 10, 14/pp. 158-163)
07 Dec 1869
Legislature again authorized creation of POWELL from SULLIVAN and three other counties; creation did not take effect; boundary description was identical to that proposed in 1854. (Tenn. Acts 1869, 36th assy., 1st sess., pub., ch. 30, secs. 1-2, 4, 11-12, 19-20/pp. 33-38; McBride, 9)
14 Jul 1870
SULLIVAN lost to WASHINGTON to accommodate local residents. (Tenn. Acts 1870, 36th assy., 2d sess., ch. 1/p. 3)
03 Mar 1901
SULLIVAN lost to WASHINGTON (Va.) when the Tennessee-Virginia line through the town of Bristol was adjusted [change too small to display on interactive map; shapefile users see small_changes 1901_pt. for location]. (Van Zandt, 110)

WASHINGTON

24 Dec 1777
WASHINGTON created by North Carolina from Washington District and non-county area; included all of present Tennessee and part of North Carolina. Residents in North Holston and Carters Valley settlements (in present Tennessee) still considered themselves part of WASHINGTON (Va.); the precise location of the boundary between WASHINGTON and Virginia was not demarcated. (N.C. St. Recs., 24:ch. 31/pp. 141-142)
10 Nov 1779
WASHINGTON lost to creation of SULLIVAN. (N.C. St. Recs., 24:ch. 29/pp. 300-302)
17 May 1783
WASHINGTON lost to creation of DAVIDSON and GREENE. (N.C. St. Recs., 24:ch. 51-52/pp. 539-540 and ch. 2, sec. 5/p. 479)
01 Mar 1785
WASHINGTON lost to creation of WAYNE (State of Franklin); North Carolina did not recognize the legitimacy of WAYNE and its precise boundaries are unknown [not mapped]. (Jordan, "Evolution . . . Hawkins and Sumner," 4-5, 8; Ramsey, 293-295; Williams, Samuel C., Lost State of Franklin, 55-58)
06 Dec 1788
WASHINGTON lost to SULLIVAN. (N.C. St. Recs., 24:ch. 29/p. 974)
26 May 1790
The United States created the Territory of the United States South of the River Ohio (Southwest Territory), covering the territory ceded in April 1790 by North Carolina (area of present Tennessee). WASHINGTON became a county in the Southwest Territory. WASHINGTON lost its eastern tip to the North Carolina side of the boundary. (Terr. Papers U.S., 4:18-19; U.S. Stat., vol. 1, ch. 14[1790], p. 123)
09 Apr 1796
WASHINGTON lost to creation of CARTER. (Tenn. Acts 1796, 1st assy., 1st sess., ch. 31, sec. 1/p. 100)
01 Jun 1796
WASHINGTON became a county in the newly-established state of Tennessee. (U.S. Stat., vol. 1, ch. 47[1796], pp. 491-492; Folmsbee, Corlew, and Mitchell 110)
02 Nov 1809
WASHINGTON lost to CARTER to accommodate local resident [location unknown, not mapped]. (Scott, ch. 27/p. 1136)
c. Dec 1835
Legislature authorized creation of POWELL from WASHINGTON and three other counties; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1835, 21st assy., 1st sess., loc., ch. 29, secs. 1-3/pp. 129-130)
c. Jan 1838
Legislature again authorized creation of POWELL from WASHINGTON and three other counties; creation did not take effect. (Tenn. Acts 1837, 22d assy., ch. 192, secs. 1-3, 15-16/pp. 277, 280-281 and ch. 199, sec. 4/p. 291)
c. Nov 1839
Legislature again authorized creation of POWELL from WASHINGTON and three other counties; this creation was disallowed by the Tennessee Supreme Court in 1841. (Tenn. Acts 1839, 23d assy., ch. 15, secs. 1-2, 4-5, 16/pp. 25-27, 30; "Bradley v. Commissioners" in Tenn. Rpts., 21:428-433 [Humphreys, vol. 2])
02 Jan 1846
WASHINGTON exchanged with SULLIVAN to accommodate local residents [location of WASHINGTON gain unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1845, 26th assy., ch. 47/p. 101)
02 Mar 1854
Legislature again authorized creation of POWELL from WASHINGTON and three other counties; creation did not take effect. It is unclear whether any of WASHINGTON was actually included within the boundaries as described. (Tenn. Acts 1853, 30th assy., ch. 89, secs. 1-3, 8, 10, 14/pp. 158-163)
07 Dec 1869
Legislature again authorized creation of POWELL from WASHINGTON and three other counties; creation did not take effect; boundary description was identical to that proposed in 1854. (Tenn. Acts 1869, 36th assy., 1st sess., pub., ch. 30, secs. 1-2, 4, 11-12, 19-20/pp. 33-38; McBride, 9)
17 Jun 1870
WASHINGTON lost to CARTER to accommodate local resident [location unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1870, 36th assy., 2d sess., ch. 21/p. 36)
14 Jul 1870
WASHINGTON gained from SULLIVAN to accommodate local residents. (Tenn. Acts 1870, 36th assy., 2d sess., ch. 1/p. 3)
21 Oct 1875
WASHINGTON lost to creation of UNICOI. (Tenn. Acts 1875, 39th assy., ch. 68, secs. 14-15/p. 86; Goodspeed [K], 905)
05 Apr 1881
WASHINGTON gained from UNICOI to accommodate local residents [change too small to display on interactive map; shapefile users see small_changes 1881_pt. for location]. WASHINGTON lost to GREENE. (Tenn. Acts 1881, 42d assy., 1st sess., ch. 147/p. 196; ch. 145/p. 194)
18 Mar 1891
WASHINGTON gained from GREENE to accommodate local residents [locations unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1891, 47th assy., ch. 142/p. 313)
14 May 1895
WASHINGTON gained from GREENE to accommodate local resident. (Tenn. Acts 1895, 49th assy., ch. 176/p. 375)
07 Apr 1899
WASHINGTON lost to CARTER to accommodate local resident [repealed 17 May 1915; location unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1899, 51st assy., ch. 171/p. 319)
17 May 1915
WASHINGTON gained from CARTER to accommodate local resident [repealed act of 7 April 1899; location unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1915, 59th assy., priv., ch. 646/p. 2114)
28 Feb 1972
WASHINGTON lost to GREENE to accommodate local resident. (Tenn. Acts 1972, 87th assy., 2d reg. sess., pub., ch. 450/p. 19)
13 Apr 1973
WASHINGTON lost to GREENE to accommodate local resident [location unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1973, 88th assy., 1st reg. sess., pub., ch. 79, sec. 1/p. 186)
19 Apr 1973
WASHINGTON gained from GREENE to accommodate local residents [locations unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1973, 88th assy., 1st reg. sess., pub., ch. 102, sec. 1/p. 274)
17 Apr 1980
WASHINGTON gained small areas from GREENE [locations unknown, not mapped]. (Tenn. Acts 1980, 91st assy., 2d reg. sess., pub., ch. 795, sec. 1/p. 918)
22 Apr 1982
WASHINGTON gained from GREENE to accommodate local resident [location unknown not mapped; map depicts net changes in WASHINGTON-GREENE line 1891-1982]. (Tenn. Acts 1982, 92d assy., 2d reg. sess., pub., ch. 855/p. 514)

WAYNE (State of Franklin)

01 Mar 1785
The First General Assembly of the State of Franklin convened in Jonesborough, Tenn., and recognized the three existing North Carolina counties located in eastern Tennessee (GREENE, SULLIVAN, and WASHINGTON) and created four new counties; the text of the acts is not extant and the precise boundaries of the counties are unknown. North Carolina did not recognize the legitimacy of these counties and sought to regain control of the area. WAYNE (State of Franklin) created from WASHINGTON and WILKES (N.C.) in the vicinity of present CARTER and JOHNSON [not mapped] (Jordan, "Evolution . . . Hawkins and Sumner," 4-5, 8; Ramsey, 293-295; Williams, Samuel C., Lost State of Franklin, 55-58)
01 Feb 1789
WAYNE eliminated with all other counties in the State of Franklin when John Sevier, governor of the State of Franklin, formally swore allegiance to North Carolina, effectively ending Franklin's operation and signaling the region's return to North Carolina control. (Folmsbee, Corlew, and Mitchell, 88-90; Williams, Samuel Cole, Lost State of Franklin, 213-225)

Acts 1915, 59th assy., priv., ch. 477/p. 1560; ch. 542/p. 1736; ch. 656/p. 2137)
in Dec 1917
Tennessee Supreme Court upheld act of 17 May 1915 (ch. 477) and ruled that the Ravenscroft area, which was transferred from PUTNAM to WHITE by said act, had actually always been part of WHITE, thus invalidating the 1902 boundary survey. Supreme Court also upheld ruling of PUTNAM Chancery Court which overturned act of 17 May 1915 (ch. 656). ("Putnam County v. White County" in Tenn. Rpts., 140:19-33)

WISDOM (proposed)

23 Mar 1875
Legislature authorized creation of WISDOM from HARDEMAN, HENDERSON, McNAIRY, and MADISON; creation did not take effect. CHESTER was created in this same general area in 1882. (Tenn. Acts 1875, 39th assy., ch. 68, secs. 1-2, 4/pp. 83-84; McBride, 9)
